<!-- Per MOS:BOLDTITLE and WP:SBE, neither the article's title nor related text appears in bold. -->

The 2013–2016 [[epidemic]] of [[Ebola virus disease]], centered in [[West Africa|Western Africa]], was the most widespread [[List of Ebola outbreaks|outbreak of the disease in history]]. It caused major loss of life and [[Socioeconomics|socioeconomic]] disruption in the region, mainly in [[Ebola virus epidemic in Guinea|Guinea]], [[Ebola virus epidemic in Liberia|Liberia]] and [[Ebola virus epidemic in Sierra Leone|Sierra Leone]]. The first cases were recorded in Guinea in December 2013; later, the disease spread to neighbouring Liberia and Sierra Leone,<ref name=":1" /> with minor outbreaks occurring  in [[Ebola virus disease in Nigeria|Nigeria]] and [[Ebola virus disease in Mali|Mali]].<ref name="WHO2015_01_211">{{cite report|url=https://afro.who.int/news/end-ebola-transmission-guinea|title=End of Ebola transmission in Guinea|publisher=WHO Regional Office for Africa|language=en|access-date=30 October 2018}}</ref><ref name="health-ebola-mali-idINL6N0T15CN20141112">{{cite news|date=12 November 2014|title=Update: Mali confirms new case of Ebola, locks down Bamako clinic|work=Reuters|url=http://in.reuters.com/article/health-ebola-mali-idINL6N0T15CN20141112|access-date=15 November 2014}}</ref> Secondary infections of medical workers occurred in the [[Ebola virus cases in the United States|United States]] and [[Ebola virus disease in Spain|Spain]].<ref name="El_Mundo">{{cite news|date=6 October 2014|title=Una enfermera que atendió al misionero fallecido García Viejo, contagiada de ébola|language=es|newspaper=El Mundo|url=http://www.elmundo.es/madrid/2014/10/06/5432bb62e2704e347a8b4577.html?a=a733fe5654cd56f5e1d50d769a9b4204&t=1412616936|access-date=6 October 2014}}</ref><ref name="Ebola_Outbreak_total_WHO_8_Oct">{{cite report|url=http://apps.who.int/iris/bitstream/10665/136020/1/roadmapsitrep_8Oct2014_eng.pdf?ua=1|title=Ebola outbreak situation report|date=8 October 2014|publisher=WHO|access-date=15 October 2014|format=PDF}}</ref> In addition, isolated cases were recorded in [[Senegal]],<ref name="sitrep_7Nov2014">{{cite report|url=http://apps.who.int/iris/bitstream/10665/137592/1/roadmapsitrep_7Nov2014_eng.pdf?ua=1|title=Ebola response roadmap situation report update|date=7 November 2014|publisher=WHO|access-date=7 November 2014|format=PDF}}</ref> the [[Ebola virus disease in the United Kingdom|United Kingdom]] and [[Italy]].<ref name="WHO2014_12_28">{{cite report|url=http://apps.who.int/ebolaweb/sitreps/20141231/20141231.pdf|title=Ebola response roadmap situation report|date=31 December 2014|publisher=WHO|quote=The reported case fatality rate in the three intense-transmission countries among all cases for whom a definitive outcome is known is 71%.|access-date=1 January 2015|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20141231222250/http://apps.who.int/ebolaweb/sitreps/20141231/20141231.pdf|archive-date=31 December 2014|url-status=dead}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|title=Ebola virus disease – Italy|url=https://www.who.int/csr/don/13-may-2015-ebola/en/|url-status=dead|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150516012204/http://www.who.int/csr/don/13-may-2015-ebola/en/|archive-date=16 May 2015|access-date=28 October 2016|publisher=WHO}}</ref> The number of cases peaked in October 2014 and then began to decline gradually, following the commitment of substantial international resources. <section begin="casesasof" />

It caused significant mortality, with a considerable [[case fatality rate]].<ref name=":1">{{cite journal |doi=10.1056/NEJMoa1411100 |title=Ebola virus disease in West Africa – the first 9 months of the epidemic and forward projections |journal=New England Journal of Medicine |date=23 September 2014 |author=WHO Ebola Response Team|quote=...&nbsp;we estimate that the case fatality rate is 70.8% (95% confidence interval [CI], 69 to 73) among persons with known clinical outcome of infection. |volume=371 |issue=16 |pages=1481–1495 |pmid=25244186 |pmc=4235004}}</ref><ref name="WHO2014_12_28" /><ref name="cfrebolavirus">{{cite web|url=http://epidemic.bio.ed.ac.uk/ebolavirus_fatality_rate|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140829075833/http://epidemic.bio.ed.ac.uk/ebolavirus_fatality_rate|url-status=dead|archive-date=29 August 2014|title=Case Fatality Rate for ebolavirus|date=2015|publisher= University of Edinburgh|access-date=28 January 2015}}</ref>{{refn|group=note|name=cfr|The mortality (number of dead per number of healthy per time frame) recorded in Liberia up to 26 August 2014 was 70%.<ref name="cfrebolavirus" /> However, due to the estimation method used, the estimated case fatality rate (70.8%) for this particular epidemic differs from the actual ratio between the number of deaths and the number of cases.}} By the end of the epidemic, 28,616 people had been infected; of these, 11,310 had died, for a case-fatality rate of 40%.<ref>{{cite news|last1=Wappes |first1=Jim |title=US health worker monitored as DRC Ebola nears 600 cases |url=http://www.cidrap.umn.edu/news-perspective/2018/12/us-health-worker-monitored-drc-ebola-nears-600-cases |publisher=CIDRAP |access-date=23 January 2019 |language=en}}</ref> {{As of|2016|5|08}}<section end="casesasof" />, the [[World Health Organization]] (WHO) and respective governments reported a total of <section begin="cases" />28,646<section end="cases" /> suspected cases and <section begin="deaths" />11,323<section end="deaths" /> deaths<section begin="caserefs" /><ref name="08who2016">{{cite report|url=https://www.who.int/en/news-room/fact-sheets/detail/ebola-virus-disease|title=Ebola virus disease|publisher=World Health Organization|access-date=6 June 2019}}</ref><section end="caserefs" /> (39.5%), though the WHO believes that this substantially understates the magnitude of the outbreak.<ref name="CDC Estimating future number of cases">{{cite journal |url=https://www.cdc.gov/mmwr/preview/mmwrhtml/su63e0923a1.htm | title=Estimating the future number of cases in the Ebola epidemic – Liberia and Sierra Leone, 2014–2015 | journal=Morbidity and Mortality Weekly Report |date=26 September 2014 | author=Meltzer, Martin I. | author2=Atkins, Charisma Y. | author3=Santibanez, Scott | author4=Knust, Barbara | author5=Petersen, Brett W. | author6=Ervin, Elizabeth D. | author7=Nichol, Stuart T. | author8=Damon, Inger K. | author9=Washington, Michael L. | volume=63 | issue=3 | pages=1–14 | pmid=25254986 | display-authors=3}}</ref><ref name="HP New cases 10,000 per week">{{cite magazine|last1=Worl|first1=Justin|title=New Ebola Cases Could Hit 10,000 Per Week|url=http://time.com/3505982/ebola-new-cases-world-health-organization/|access-date=28 October 2016|magazine=Time|date=2014}}</ref>

On 8 August 2014, a [[Public Health Emergency of International Concern]] was declared<ref>{{cite report|title= Statement on the 1st meeting of the IHR Emergency Committee on the 2014 Ebola outbreak in West Africa |url=https://www.who.int/mediacentre/news/statements/2014/ebola-20140808/en/ |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140808155521/http://www.who.int/mediacentre/news/statements/2014/ebola-20140808/en/ |url-status=dead |archive-date=8 August 2014 |publisher=WHO |access-date=13 January 2019}}</ref> and on 29 March 2016, the WHO terminated the Public Health Emergency of International Concern status of the outbreak.<ref name=EmergencyEnd/><ref>{{cite report|title=Interim advice on the sexual transmission of the Ebola virus disease|url=https://www.who.int/reproductivehealth/topics/rtis/ebola-virus-semen/en/|publisher=WHO|access-date=28 October 2016}}</ref><ref name="who.int1">{{cite report|url=https://www.who.int/dg/speeches/2016/executive-board-138/en/|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160126084948/http://www.who.int/dg/speeches/2016/executive-board-138/en/|url-status=dead|archive-date=26 January 2016|title=WHO Director-General addresses the Executive Board|publisher=WHO|access-date=27 January 2016}}</ref> Subsequent flare-ups occurred; the epidemic was finally declared over on 9 June 2016, 42 days after the last case tested negative on 28 April 2016 in [[Monrovia]].<ref>{{cite report|last1=WHO|title=Situation Report Ebola|date=10 June 2016|url=http://apps.who.int/iris/bitstream/10665/208883/1/ebolasitrep_10Jun2016_eng.pdf|publisher=WHO|access-date=11 November 2016}}</ref>

The outbreak left about 17,000 survivors of the disease, many of whom report post-recovery symptoms termed [[post-Ebola syndrome]], often severe enough to require medical care for months or even years. An additional cause for concern is the apparent ability of the virus to "hide" in a recovered survivor's body for an extended period of time and then become active months or years later, either in the same individual or in a sexual partner.<ref name="Scientific American">{{cite magazine| url=http://www.scientificamerican.com/article/why-ebola-survivors-struggle-with-new-symptoms/ | title=Why Ebola Survivors Struggle with New Symptoms | magazine=Scientific American | date=29 February 2016 | access-date=9 September 2016 | author=Yasmin, Seema}}</ref> In December 2016, the WHO announced that a two-year trial of the [[rVSV-ZEBOV vaccine]] appeared to offer protection from the variant of EBOV responsible for the Western Africa outbreak. The vaccine is considered to be effective and is the only prophylactic which offers protection; hence, 300,000 doses have been stockpiled.<ref name="ReferenceA">{{cite journal|last1=Geisbert|first1=Thomas W.|title=First Ebola virus vaccine to protect human beings?|journal=The Lancet|volume=389|issue=10068|pages=479–480|date=December 2016|doi=10.1016/S0140-6736(16)32618-6|pmid=28017402|doi-access=free}}</ref><ref name="PBS NewsHour">{{Cite news |url=https://www.pbs.org/newshour/bb/ebola-vaccine-results-encouraging-preliminary/ |title=Ebola vaccine results are encouraging – but preliminary |date=23 December 2016 |publisher=PBS}}</ref> rVSV-ZEBOV received regulatory approval in 2019.<ref name=EMA_ZEBOV>{{cite web |url=https://www.ema.europa.eu/en/medicines/human/EPAR/ervebo |title=Ervebo |publisher=EMA |date=12 December 2019 |access-date=2 February 2020}}</ref><ref name=FDA_ZEBOV>{{cite web |url=https://www.fda.gov/news-events/press-announcements/first-fda-approved-vaccine-prevention-ebola-virus-disease-marking-critical-milestone-public-health |title=First FDA-approved vaccine for the prevention of Ebola virus disease, marking a critical milestone in public health preparedness and response |publisher=FDA |date=19 December 2019 |access-date=2 February 2020}}</ref>

== Overview ==

Ebola virus disease (commonly known as "Ebola")  was first described in 1976 in two simultaneous outbreaks in the [[Democratic Republic of the Congo]] and what is now [[South Sudan]].<ref>{{cite journal | pmc = 2395567 | pmid=307456 | volume=56 | issue=2 | title=Ebola haemorrhagic fever in Zaire, 1976 | year=1978 | journal=Bulletin of the World Health Organization | pages=271–293}}</ref> The 2013–2016 outbreak, caused by Ebola virus (EBOV),<ref>{{cite journal |last1=Becker |first1=Stephan |last2=Matrosovich |first2=Mikhail |last3=Krähling |first3=Verena |last4=Schudt |first4=Gordian |last5=Dietzel |first5=Erik |title=Functional Characterization of Adaptive Mutations during the West African Ebola Virus Outbreak |journal=Journal of Virology |date=15 January 2017 |volume=91 |issue=2 |pages=e01913–e01916 |doi=10.1128/JVI.01913-16 |pmid=27847361 |pmc=5215343 }}</ref> was the first anywhere in the world to reach epidemic proportions. Previous outbreaks had been brought under control in a much shorter period of time. [[Extreme poverty]], dysfunctional healthcare systems, distrust of government after years of armed conflict, and the delay in responding for several months, all contributed to the failure to control the epidemic. Other factors, per media reports, included local burial customs of washing the body and the unprecedented spread of Ebola to densely populated cities.<ref name=sitrep_24Sept2014>{{cite report|title=Ebola response roadmap situation report |url=http://apps.who.int/iris/bitstream/10665/134771/1/roadmapsitrep_24Sept2014_eng.pdf?ua=1 |format=PDF |publisher=WHO|access-date=25 September 2014|page=6}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=Runaway doctors and missing supplies cripple care in Ebola-hit Liberia |url=http://www.nbcnews.com/storyline/ebola-virus-outbreak/runaway-doctors-missing-supplies-cripple-care-ebola-hit-liberia-n220686 |work=NBC News|access-date=8 October 2014}}</ref><ref name="WHO 2014-07-03">{{cite report|url=http://www.afro.who.int/en/clusters-a-programmes/dpc/epidemic-a-pandemic-alert-and-response/outbreak-news/4216-ebola-virus-disease-west-africa-3-july-2014.html|title=Ebola virus disease, West Africa|date=3 July 2014|publisher=WHO|access-date=18 September 2014|url-status=dead|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140728210024/http://www.afro.who.int/en/clusters-a-programmes/dpc/epidemic-a-pandemic-alert-and-response/outbreak-news/4216-ebola-virus-disease-west-africa-3-july-2014.html|archive-date=28 July 2014|df=dmy-all}}</ref><ref name="Global Post">{{cite news |url=http://www.globalpost.com/dispatch/news/xinhua-news-agency/140527/8-ebola-suspects-freed-relatives-sierra-leone |title=8 Ebola suspects freed by relatives in Sierra Leone |publisher=Global Post |agency=Xinhua |date=28 May 2014 |access-date=21 June 2014 |archive-date=31 May 2014 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140531084044/http://www.globalpost.com/dispatch/news/xinhua-news-agency/140527/8-ebola-suspects-freed-relatives-sierra-leone |url-status=dead }}</ref><ref name="Today Health">{{cite news |url=http://www.today.com/health/growing-ebola-outbreak-threatens-overwhelm-volunteers-2D79775266 |title=Growing Ebola outbreak threatens to overwhelm volunteers |publisher=Today Health |date=8 June 2014 |access-date=21 June 2014}}</ref>
[[File:2014 ebola virus epidemic in West Africa.svg|thumb|upright=1.5|Map showing death statistics as of 2014]]
As the outbreak progressed, the media reports, many hospitals, short on both staff and supplies, were overwhelmed and closed down, leading some health experts to state that the inability to treat other medical needs may have been causing "an additional death toll [that is] likely to exceed that of the outbreak itself".<ref name=":2">{{cite news|url=https://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/africa/ebola-outbreak-deaths-from-malaria-and-other-diseases-could-soar-while-africas-overstretched-healthcare-systems-fight-the-virus-expert-warns-9667362.html|title=Ebola outbreak: Deaths from malaria and other diseases could soar while Africa's over-stretched healthcare systems fight the virus, expert warns|newspaper=The Independent| date=27 October 2014|access-date=28 October 2014|author=Cooper, Charlie|location=London}}</ref><ref name="Diary">{{cite magazine|last1=Farmer|first1=Paul|title=Diary|url=http://www.lrb.co.uk/v36/n20/paul-farmer/diary|access-date=25 October 2014|magazine=London Review of Books|date=23 October 2014}}</ref> Hospital workers, who worked closely with the highly contagious body fluids of the victims, were especially vulnerable to contracting the virus; in August 2014, the WHO reported that ten per cent of the dead had been healthcare workers.<ref name="As Ebola outbreak surges, health officials slam international 'Coalition of Inaction'">{{cite web|url=http://www.commondreams.org/news/2014/09/03/ebola-outbreak-surges-health-officials-slam-international-coalition-inaction|title=As Ebola outbreak surges, health officials slam international 'Coalition of Inaction'|publisher=Common Dreams |date=3 September 2014 |access-date=7 September 2014 |author=McCauley, Lauren}}</ref> In September 2014, it was estimated that the affected countries' capacity for treating Ebola patients was insufficient by the equivalent of 2,122 beds; however, by December 2014 there were enough beds to treat and isolate all reported cases, although the uneven distribution of cases was resulting in serious shortfalls in some areas.<ref name="WHO2014_12_10">{{cite report |url=http://apps.who.int/iris/bitstream/10665/145198/1/roadmapsitrep_10Dec2014_eng.pdf?ua=1|format= PDF|title=Ebola response roadmap situation report|publisher=WHO|date=10 December 2014|access-date=11 December 2014}}</ref>

The WHO has been widely criticised for its delay in taking action to address the epidemic.<ref name="AP News">{{cite news | url=https://apnews.com/2489c78bff86463589b41f3faaea5ab2/emails-un-health-agency-resisted-declaring-ebola-emergency | title=Emails: UN health agency resisted declaring Ebola emergency | publisher=Associated Press | date=20 March 2015 | access-date=21 March 2015 |author1=Cheng, Maria |author2=Satter, Raphael }}</ref> On 8 August 2014, it declared the outbreak a [[public health emergency of international concern]].<ref name=WHO_PHEIC_8Aug2014>{{cite report |url=https://www.who.int/mediacentre/news/statements/2014/ebola-20140808/en/ |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140808155521/http://www.who.int/mediacentre/news/statements/2014/ebola-20140808/en/ |url-status=dead |archive-date=8 August 2014 |title=WHO Statement on the Meeting of the International Health Regulations Emergency Committee Regarding the 2014 Ebola Outbreak in West Africa |publisher=WHO |date=8 August 2014 |access-date=8 August 2014}}</ref> By September 2014, [[Médecins Sans Frontières|Médecins Sans Frontières/Doctors Without Borders]] (MSF), the [[non-governmental organisation]] with the largest working presence in the affected countries, had grown increasingly critical of the international response. Speaking on 3 September, the International President of MSF spoke out concerning the lack of assistance from [[United Nations]] (UN) member countries: "Six months into the worst Ebola epidemic in history, the world is losing the battle to contain it."<ref name="Ebola: the failures of the international outbreak response">{{cite news|title=Ebola: the failures of the international outbreak response |url=https://www.msf.org/ebola-failures-international-outbreak-response |publisher=Médecins Sans Frontières|access-date=5 March 2019 |language=en}}</ref>  In a 26 September statement, the WHO stated that "[t]he Ebola epidemic ravaging parts of Western Africa is the most severe acute public health emergency seen in modern times" and its Director-General called the outbreak "the largest, most complex and most severe we've ever seen".<ref name="UN senior leaders outline needs for global Ebola response">{{cite press release |url=https://www.who.int/mediacentre/news/releases/2014/ebola-response-needs/en/ |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140907161412/http://www.who.int/mediacentre/news/releases/2014/ebola-response-needs/en/ |url-status=dead |archive-date=7 September 2014 |title=UN senior leaders outline needs for global Ebola response |publisher=WHO |date=3 September 2014 |access-date=7 September 2014}}</ref> In March 2015, the [[United Nations Development Group]] reported that due to a decrease in trade, closing of borders, flight cancellations, and drop in foreign investment and tourism activity fuelled by stigma, the epidemic had resulted in vast economic consequences in both the affected areas in Western Africa and even in other African nations with no cases of Ebola.<ref name="auto2">{{cite press release|url=http://www.undp.org/content/undp/en/home/presscenter/pressreleases/2015/03/12/west-african-economies-feeling-ripple-effects-of-ebola-says-un.html|title=West African economies feeling ripple effects of Ebola, says UN|publisher=United Nations Development Programme|date=12 March 2015|access-date=20 March 2015|archive-date=18 March 2015|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150318230625/http://www.undp.org/content/undp/en/home/presscenter/pressreleases/2015/03/12/west-african-economies-feeling-ripple-effects-of-ebola-says-un.html|url-status=dead}}</ref>

On 28 January 2015, the WHO reported that for the first time since the week ending 29 June 2014, there had been fewer than 100 new confirmed cases reported in a week in the three most-affected countries. The response to the epidemic then moved to a second phase, as the focus shifted from slowing transmission to ending the epidemic.<ref name="WHO5feb">{{cite report|url=http://apps.who.int/ebola/en/ebola-situation-report/situation-reports/ebola-situation-report-28-january-2015|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150131111021/http://apps.who.int/ebola/en/ebola-situation-report/situation-reports/ebola-situation-report-28-january-2015|url-status=dead|archive-date=31 January 2015|title=Ebola situation report |date=28 January 2015|publisher=WHO|access-date=5 February 2015}}</ref> On 8 April 2015, the WHO reported a total of only 30 confirmed cases,<ref name="WHO8apil">{{cite report|url=http://apps.who.int/iris/bitstream/10665/161244/1/roadmapsitrep_8Apr2015_eng.pdf?ua=1&ua=1|title=Ebola situation report|date=8 April 2015|publisher=WHO|access-date=14 April 2015}}</ref> and the weekly update for 29 July reported only seven new cases.<ref name=":4">{{cite web|url=http://www.cidrap.umn.edu/news-perspective/2015/07/ebola-numbers-drop-sharply-guinea-sierra-leone|title=Ebola numbers drop sharply in Guinea, Sierra Leone|publisher=CIDRAP|access-date=30 July 2015}}</ref>  Cases continued to gradually dwindle and on 7 October 2015, all three of the most seriously affected countries, per media reports, recorded their first joint week without any new cases.<ref name=":9">{{cite news|url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-africa-34471234|title=Ebola countries record first week with no new cases|work=BBC News|access-date=8 October 2015|date=2015-10-07}}</ref> However, as of late 2015, while the large-scale epidemic had ended, according to media reports, sporadic new cases were still being recorded, frustrating hopes that the epidemic could be declared over.<ref name=":10">{{cite news|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2015/nov/20/ebola-case-in-liberia-confirmed-by-who|title=Liberian official urges calm as three new Ebola cases confirmed|newspaper=The Guardian|access-date=21 November 2015}}</ref>

On 31 July 2015, the WHO announced "an extremely promising development" in the search for an effective vaccine for Ebola virus disease. While the vaccine had shown high efficacy in individuals, more conclusive evidence was needed regarding its capacity to protect populations through [[herd immunity]].<ref name="auto4">{{cite journal |last1=Henao-Restrepo |first1=Ana Maria |last2=Longini |first2=Ira M |last3=Egger |first3=Matthias |last4=Dean |first4=Natalie E
 |author-link4=Natalie Dean |last5=Edmunds |first5=W John |last6=Camacho |first6=Anton |last7=Carroll |first7=Miles W |last8=Doumbia |first8=Moussa |last9=Draguez |first9=Bertrand |last10=Duraffour |first10=Sophie |last11=Enwere |first11=Godwin |last12=Grais |first12=Rebecca |last13=Gunther |first13=Stephan |last14=Hossmann |first14=Stefanie |last15=Kondé |first15=Mandy Kader |last16=Kone |first16=Souleymane |last17=Kuisma |first17=Eeva |last18=Levine |first18=Myron M |last19=Mandal |first19=Sema |last20=Norheim |first20=Gunnstein |last21=Riveros |first21=Ximena |last22=Soumah |first22=Aboubacar |last23=Trelle |first23=Sven |last24=Vicari |first24=Andrea S |last25=Watson |first25=Conall H |last26=Kéïta |first26=Sakoba |last27=Kieny |first27=Marie Paule |last28=Røttingen |first28=John-Arne |title=Efficacy and effectiveness of an rVSV-vectored vaccine expressing Ebola surface glycoprotein: interim results from the Guinea ring vaccination cluster-randomised trial |journal=The Lancet |date=August 2015 |volume=386 |issue=9996 |pages=857–866 |doi=10.1016/S0140-6736(15)61117-5|pmid=26248676|hdl=10144/575218 |s2cid=40830730 |hdl-access=free }}</ref><ref name="auto5">{{cite press release |title=World on the verge of an effective Ebola vaccine |url=http://who.int/mediacentre/news/releases/2015/effective-ebola-vaccine/en/ |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150731200521/http://www.who.int/mediacentre/news/releases/2015/effective-ebola-vaccine/en/ |url-status=dead |archive-date=31 July 2015 |publisher=WHO |access-date=31 July 2015}}</ref>  In August 2015, after substantial progress in reducing the scale of the epidemic, the WHO held a meeting to work out a "Comprehensive care plan for Ebola survivors" and identify research needed to optimise clinical care and social well-being.  Stating that "the Ebola outbreak has decimated families, health systems, economies, and social structures", the WHO called the aftermath of the epidemic "an emergency within an emergency."  Of special concern is recent research that shows some Ebola survivors experience a so-called "post-Ebola Syndrome", with symptoms so severe that survivors may require medical care for months and even years.<ref name="WHO20150807">{{cite press release | url=http://www.afro.who.int/en/sierra-leone/press-materials/item/7908-an-emergency-within-an-emergency-caring-for-ebola-survivors.html | title=An emergency within an emergency: caring for Ebola survivors | publisher=WHO | date=7 August 2015 | access-date=19 August 2015 | url-status=dead | archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150813163313/http://www.afro.who.int/en/sierra-leone/press-materials/item/7908-an-emergency-within-an-emergency-caring-for-ebola-survivors.html | archive-date=13 August 2015 | df=dmy-all }}</ref><ref name="post">{{cite journal |last1=Burki |first1=Talha Khan |title=Post-Ebola syndrome |journal=The Lancet Infectious Diseases |date=1 July 2016 |volume=16 |issue=7 |pages=780–781 |doi=10.1016/S1473-3099(15)00259-5 |pmid=27352759 |doi-access=free }}</ref>  As the main epidemic was coming to an end in December 2015, the UN announced that 22,000 children had lost one or both parents to Ebola.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.un.org/apps/news/story.asp?NewsID=52913 |title=UN declares end to Ebola virus transmission in Guinea; first time all three host countries free <!--|author=no by-line.--> |publisher=UN News Center |access-date=30 December 2015}}</ref>  On 29 March 2016, the Director-General of WHO terminated the Public Health Emergency of International Concern status of the Western African Ebola virus epidemic.<ref name=EmergencyEnd/>

== Epidemiology ==

=== Outbreak ===
{{See also|Ebola virus epidemic in West Africa timeline}}
[[File:Ebola Outbreak Map (ongoing).png|thumb|upright=1.5|Ebola outbreak worldwide{{legend|#eb1c23|Widespread outbreak}}{{legend|#ff7e29|Limited outbreak}}{{legend|#ffee00|Isolated cases}}{{legend|#00a1e6|Medically evacuated cases}}]]
It is generally believed that a one or two-year-old boy,<ref name="NYT122914">{{cite news|author1=Kevin Sack |author2=Sheri Fink |author3=Pam Belluck |author4=Adam Nossiter|title=How Ebola Roared Back|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2014/12/30/health/how-ebola-roared-back.html|access-date=30 December 2014|newspaper=The New York Times|date=29 December 2014|quote=The messages about don't touch the dead, wash your hands, if somebody is sick, leave them—these were all strange things, completely contrary to our tradition and culture.<!--Anchor cite of important article, do not remove-->}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.cnn.com/2014/10/28/health/ebola-patient-zero/index.html|title=Ebola: Patient zero was a toddler in Guinea|author1=Holly Yan |author2=Esprit Smith|website=CNN|date=28 October 2014|access-date=2020-04-14}}</ref> later identified as [[Emile Ouamouno]], who died in December 2013 in the village of [[Meliandou|Méliandou]], [[Guéckédou Prefecture]], [[Guinea]], was the [[index case]] of the Western African epidemic.<ref name="Baize-2014" /> Scientists have deduced that bats are involved in the spread of the virus,<ref>{{cite news|title=Scientists Discover Ebola Virus in West African Bat |url=https://www.mailman.columbia.edu/public-health-now/news/scientists-discover-ebola-virus-west-african-bat |work=www.mailman.columbia.edu |publisher=Columbia University Mailman School of Public Health|access-date=26 January 2019}}</ref> and, incidentally, the boy's home was in the vicinity of a large colony of [[Angolan free-tailed bat]]s, according to media reports.<ref name=mg>{{cite news |agency=AFP |date=30 December 2014 | title=Hollow tree in Guinea was Ebola's Ground Zero, scientists say |url=http://mgafrica.com/article/2014-12-30-hollow-tree-in-guinea-was-ebolas-ground-zero-scientists-say |publisher=Mail & Guardian Africa |access-date=1 January 2016}}</ref> His mother, sister, and grandmother, per media reports later became ill with similar symptoms and also died; people infected by these initial cases spread the disease to other villages.<ref name="tracingebola">{{cite news | author=Grady, Denise | author2=Fink, Sheri | title=Tracing Ebola's Breakout to an African 2-Year-Old | newspaper=The New York Times | date=9 August 2014  |access-date= 11 April 2015| url=https://www.nytimes.com/2014/08/10/world/africa/tracing-ebolas-breakout-to-an-african-2-year-old.html }}</ref><ref name=BBC-world-africa-30199004>{{cite news|url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-africa-30199004|title=How world's worst Ebola outbreak began with one boy's death|author=Nassos Stylianou |date=27 November 2014 |access-date= 11 April 2015|work=BBC News}}</ref> There was knowledge of ''Tai Forest virus'' in Côte d'Ivoire, which had resulted in one human transmission in 1994. Thus, these early cases were diagnosed as other conditions more common to the area and the disease had several months to spread before it became recognised as Ebola.<ref name="Baize-2014">{{cite journal|title= Emergence of Zaire Ebola Virus Disease in Guinea&nbsp;– Preliminary Report|date= 16 April 2014 |doi=10.1056/NEJMoa1404505 |last1= Baize |first1= Sylvain |last2= Pannetier |first2= Delphine |last3= Oestereich|first3= Lisa|last4= Rieger|first4= Toni|journal= New England Journal of Medicine |pmid= 24738640 |volume= 371 |issue= 15 |pages= 1418–1425|s2cid= 34198809 |url= https://semanticscholar.org/paper/29bafbdb9b461edc7f705777a6672000570b896c }}</ref><ref name="tracingebola" />
[[File:ebola cases.gif|thumb|upright=1.5|Monthly aggregate Ebola cases in the Western Africa epidemic 2014–15]]
[[File:ebola deaths.gif|thumb|upright=1.5|Monthly aggregate Ebola deaths in the Western Africa epidemic 2014–15]]
On 25 March 2014, the WHO indicated that [[Ministry of Health (Guinea)|Guinea's Ministry of Health]] had reported an outbreak of Ebola virus disease in four southeastern districts, and that suspected cases in the neighbouring countries of [[Liberia]] and [[Sierra Leone]] were being investigated. In Guinea, a total of 86 suspected cases, including 59 deaths, had been reported as of 24 March.<ref name=Previous_Updates_2014_West_Africa_Outbreak>{{cite report|url=https://www.cdc.gov/vhf/ebola/outbreaks/guinea/recent_updates.html |title=Previous Updates: 2014 West Africa Outbreak |publisher=CDC|access-date= 11 April 2015}}</ref> By late May, the outbreak had spread to [[Conakry]], Guinea's capital—a city of about two million people.<ref name=Previous_Updates_2014_West_Africa_Outbreak /> On 28 May, the total number of reported cases had reached 281, with 186 deaths.<ref name=Previous_Updates_2014_West_Africa_Outbreak />

In Liberia, the disease was reported in four counties by mid-April 2014 and cases in Liberia's capital [[Monrovia]] were reported in mid-June.<ref name="DON 16APR14">{{cite report|url= http://www.afro.who.int/en/clusters-a-programmes/dpc/epidemic-a-pandemic-alert-and-response/outbreak-news/4100-ebola-virus-disease-west-africa-16-april-2014.html|title= Ebola virus disease, West Africa (Situation as of 16 April 2014)|publisher= WHO|access-date= 18 September 2014|url-status= dead|archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20141006171623/http://www.afro.who.int/en/clusters-a-programmes/dpc/epidemic-a-pandemic-alert-and-response/outbreak-news/4100-ebola-virus-disease-west-africa-16-april-2014.html|archive-date= 6 October 2014|df= dmy-all}}</ref> The outbreak then spread to Sierra Leone and progressed rapidly. By 17 July, the total number of suspected cases in the country stood at 442, surpassing those in Guinea and Liberia.<ref name="WHO 2014-07-18">{{cite report|url=http://www.afro.who.int/en/clusters-a-programmes/dpc/epidemic-a-pandemic-alert-and-response/outbreak-news/4225-ebola-virus-disease-west-africa-18-july-2014.html|title=Ebola virus disease, West Africa|date=18 July 2014|publisher=WHO|access-date=18 September 2014|url-status=dead|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140725195212/http://www.afro.who.int/en/clusters-a-programmes/dpc/epidemic-a-pandemic-alert-and-response/outbreak-news/4225-ebola-virus-disease-west-africa-18-july-2014.html|archive-date=25 July 2014|df=dmy-all}}</ref> By 20 July, additional cases of the disease had been reported by the media in the [[Bo District]], while the first case in [[Freetown]], Sierra Leone's capital, was reported in late July.<ref name="BBC_Freetown">{{cite news |url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-africa-28485041 |title=Sierra Leone hunts Ebola patient kidnapped in Freetown |work=BBC News |date=25 July 2014 |access-date=27 July 2014}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-africa-28505061 |title=Ebola outbreak: Sierra Leone escaped patient dies |work=BBC News |date=27 July 2014 |access-date=27 July 2014}}</ref>

As the epidemic progressed, a small outbreak occurred in Nigeria that resulted in 20 cases and another in Mali with 7&nbsp;cases. Four other countries (Senegal, Spain, the United Kingdom and the United States of America) also reported cases imported from Western Africa, with widespread and intense transmission.<ref name=":5">{{cite report | url=https://www.who.int/csr/disease/ebola/situation-reports/en/?m=20141112&file=sitreps/20141112/20141112.html | archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20141112221345/http://www.who.int/csr/disease/ebola/situation-reports/en/?m=20141112&file=sitreps/20141112/20141112.html | url-status=dead | archive-date=12 November 2014 | title= Ebola response roadmap situation report | publisher= WHO | date= 12 November 2014 | access-date= 16 November 2014}}</ref><ref name="WHO2014_11_23">{{cite report |url= http://apps.who.int/iris/bitstream/10665/144498/1/roadmapsitrep_26Nov2014_eng.pdf?ua=1 |title= Ebola response roadmap situation report |publisher= WHO|date=26 November 2014 |access-date = 27 November 2014}}</ref><ref name="WHO2014_11_30">{{cite report |url= http://apps.who.int/gho/data/view.ebola-sitrep.ebola-summary-20141202?lang=en |title= Situation summary Data published on 2 December 2014|publisher= WHO|date= 2 December 2014|access-date = 2 December 2014}}</ref>

On 31 March 2015, one year after the first report of the outbreak, the total number of cases was in excess of 25,000—with over 10,000&nbsp;deaths.<ref name="WHO2015_03_31">{{cite report|title=Ebola data and statistics|url=http://apps.who.int/gho/data/view.ebola-sitrep.ebola-summary-20150331?lang=en |publisher=WHO|access-date=28 October 2016}}</ref>

As the epidemic waned, following international control efforts, the edition of 8 April 2015 of the WHO's ''Ebola Situation Reports'' stated that a total of 30 cases were reported<ref>{{cite report|title=Ebola Situation Report |date=8 April 2015 |url=http://apps.who.int/ebola/current-situation/ebola-situation-report-8-april-2015|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150412004358/http://apps.who.int/ebola/current-situation/ebola-situation-report-8-april-2015|url-status=dead|archive-date=12 April 2015|publisher=WHO|access-date=29 October 2016}}</ref> and on 29 July 2015, the WHO weekly update reported only 7 cases—the lowest in more than a year.<ref name=":4" />  In October 2015, the WHO recorded its first week without any new cases,<ref name=":9" /> and while the large-scale epidemic appeared to have ended by late 2015, sporadic new cases continued to be reported.<ref name=":10" /><ref>{{cite report|url=https://www.who.int/csr/disease/ebola/flare-up-liberia/en/|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20151125011914/http://www.who.int/csr/disease/ebola/flare-up-liberia/en/|url-status=dead|archive-date=25 November 2015|title= Flare up of Ebola in Liberia|publisher= WHO|access-date= 26 November 2015}}</ref>

On 14 January 2016, after all the previously infected countries had been declared Ebola-free, the WHO reported that "all known chains of transmission have been stopped in Western Africa", but cautioned that further small outbreaks of the disease could occur in the future.<ref>{{cite news|title=West Africa declared free of Ebola transmission, but UN health agency warns new flare-ups possible |url=https://news.un.org/en/story/2016/01/519932-west-africa-declared-free-ebola-transmission-un-health-agency-warns-new-flare |work=UN News |publisher=United Nations |access-date=6 March 2019 |language=en |date=14 January 2016}}</ref> The following day, Sierra Leone confirmed its first new case since September 2015.<ref name="who.int1"/>

=== Countries that experienced widespread transmission ===
[[File:2014 West Africa Ebola virus outbreak situation map.jpg|thumb|upright=1.5|Outbreak distribution map affected part of Western Africa (17 December 2014)]]

==== Guinea ====
{{Further|Ebola virus epidemic in Guinea}}
On 25 March 2014, the WHO reported an outbreak of Ebola virus disease in four southeastern districts of Guinea with a total of 86 suspected cases, including 59 deaths, and MSF assisted the Ministry of Health by establishing Ebola treatment centres in the epicentre of the outbreak.<ref name=Previous_Updates_2014_West_Africa_Outbreak /> On 31 March, the [[U.S. Centers for Disease Control and Prevention]] (CDC) sent a five-person team to assist in the response to the outbreak.<ref name=Previous_Updates_2014_West_Africa_Outbreak /> Thinking that spread of the virus had been contained, MSF closed its treatment centres in May, leaving only a skeleton staff to handle the [[Macenta]] region. However, in late August, according to media reports, large numbers of new cases reappeared in the region.<ref name=Guinea_Ebola_Sep_Update>{{cite news |url=http://www.ctvnews.ca/health/ebola-virus-is-surging-in-places-where-it-was-beaten-back-experts-1.1996179 |title=Ebola virus is surging in places where it was beaten back: experts |publisher=CTV News |date=8 September 2014 |access-date=8 September 2014}}</ref>

In February 2015, media reported that Guinea recorded a rise in cases for the second week in a row,<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ibtimes.co.uk/ebola-cases-double-guinea-second-week-says-who-1487620|title=Ebola cases double in Guinea in second week, says WHO|publisher=International Business Times UK|access-date=12 February 2015|date=2015-02-12}}</ref>  health authorities stated that this was related to the fact that they "were only now gaining access to faraway villages", where violence had previously prevented them from entering.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.voanews.com/content/guinea-ebola-infections-double-as-hidden-cases-discovered/2631698.html|title=In Guinea, Ebola Infections Double as Hidden Cases Discovered|publisher=VOA|access-date=8 February 2015}}</ref> On 14 February, violence erupted and an Ebola treatment centre near the centre of the country was destroyed.   Guinean [[Red Cross]] teams said they had suffered an average of 10 attacks a month over the previous year;<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-health-ebola-guinea-idUSKBN0LI0G920150214|title=Crowds attack Ebola facility, health workers in Guinea|work=Reuters|access-date=19 February 2015|date=14 February 2015}}</ref> MSF reported that acceptance of Ebola education remained low and that further violence against their workers might force them to leave.<ref name="auto3">{{cite news|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-africa-32103625|title=Guinea declares Ebola 'health emergency' in five regions|work=BBC News|access-date=29 March 2015|date=2015-03-29}}</ref>

Resistance to interventions by health officials among the Guinean population remained greater than in Sierra Leone and Liberia, per media reports, raising concerns over its impact on ongoing efforts to halt the epidemic;  in mid-March, there were 95 new cases and on 28 March, and a 45-day "health emergency" was declared in 5 regions of the country.<ref name="auto3" /><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.nbcnews.com/storyline/ebola-virus-outbreak/ebola-epidemic-slows-even-more-n358376|title=Ebola Epidemic Slows Even More, WHO Says|work=NBC News|date=13 May 2015|author=Fox, Maggie}}</ref>  On 22 May, the WHO reported another rise in cases, per media reports,<ref>{{cite web|url=https://abcnews.go.com/Health/wireStory/guinea-reports-27-ebola-cases-previous-lull-31228633|title=Guinea Families Transport Bodies in Public Taxis|work=ABC News|access-date=23 May 2015}}</ref> which was believed to have been due to funeral transmissions;<ref>{{cite news |title=Guinea Ebola cases climb due to transmissions at funerals {{!}} Fox News |url=http://www.foxnews.com/health/2015/05/15/guinea-ebola-cases-climb-due-to-transmissions-at-funerals/ |access-date=27 March 2019 |work=web.archive.org |date=29 May 2015|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150529232101/http://www.foxnews.com/health/2015/05/15/guinea-ebola-cases-climb-due-to-transmissions-at-funerals/ |archive-date=29 May 2015 }}</ref>  on 25 May, six persons were placed in prison isolation after they were found travelling with the corpse of an individual who had died of the disease,<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-africa-32877392|title=Ebola crisis: Guineans jailed for putting corpse in taxi|work=BBC News|access-date=27 May 2015|date=2015-05-25}}</ref> on 1 June, it was reported that violent protests in a north Guinean town at the border with [[Guinea-Bissau]] had caused the Red Cross to withdraw its workers.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.yahoo.com/ebola-threat-guinea-bissau-rises-border-zone-heats-063714122.html|title=Ebola threat to Guinea Bissau rises as border zone heats up|date=2 June 2015|publisher=Yahoo! News|access-date=3 June 2015}}</ref>

In late June 2015, the WHO reported that "weekly case incidence has stalled at between 20 and 27 cases since the end of May, whilst cases continue to arise from unknown sources of infection, and to be detected only after [[post-mortem]] testing of community deaths".<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.un.org/apps/news/story.asp?NewsID=51245#.VYvszzfbJpg|title=United Nations News Centre|date=24 June 2015|publisher=UN News Service Section|access-date=28 June 2015}}</ref> On 29 July, a sharp decline in cases was reported,<ref name=":4" /> with only a single case, per media reports left by the end of the week,<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.nbcnews.com/storyline/ebola-virus-outbreak/ebola-rates-plummet-who-says-more-come-n404696|title=Ebola Rates Plummet, But WHO Says More to Come|author=Maggie Fox|work=NBC News|access-date=7 August 2015}}</ref> the number of cases eventually plateaued at 1 or 2 cases per week after the beginning of August.<ref>{{cite report|url=http://apps.who.int/ebola/ebola-situation-reports-archive|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150902233415/http://apps.who.int/ebola/ebola-situation-reports-archive|url-status=dead|archive-date=2 September 2015|date=17 September 2015|title=Ebola situation reports Archive |publisher=WHO |access-date=20 September 2015}}</ref> On 28 October, an additional 3 cases were reported in the [[Forécariah Prefecture]] by the WHO.<ref name="WHO2015_10_28a">{{cite report|url=http://apps.who.int/iris/bitstream/10665/191299/1/ebolasitrep_28Oct2015_eng.pdf?ua=1|title=Ebola Situation Report |publisher=WHO |date=28 October 2015}}</ref> On 6 November, a media report indicated [[Tana, Guinea|Tana]] village to be the last known place with Ebola in the country,<ref>{{cite news|title = The Last Place on Earth With Ebola: Getting Guinea to Zero|url = https://www.nytimes.com/2015/11/07/world/africa/the-last-place-on-earth-with-ebola-guineas-fight-to-get-to-zero.html|newspaper= The New York Times|date = 6 November 2015|access-date = 8 November 2015|issn = 0362-4331|first = Dionne|last = Searcey}}</ref> and on 11 November, WHO indicated that no Ebola cases were reported in Guinea; this was the first time since the epidemic began, that no cases had been reported in any country.<ref>{{cite report |title=Ebola Situation Report|date=11 November 2015|url=http://apps.who.int/ebola/current-situation/ebola-situation-report-11-november-2015 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20151111211316/http://apps.who.int/ebola/current-situation/ebola-situation-report-11-november-2015 |url-status=dead |archive-date=11 November 2015 |publisher=WHO |access-date=6 March 2019}}</ref> On 15 November, the last quarantined individuals were released, per media reports<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.yahoo.com/guinea-releases-last-68-people-ebola-quarantine-143241412.html|title=Guinea releases last 68 people from Ebola quarantine|date=14 November 2015|publisher=Yahoo! News}}</ref> and on 17 November, the last Ebola patient in Guinea—a 3-week-old baby—had recovered; the 42-day countdown toward the country being declared Ebola-free started on 17 November, the day after the patient yielded a second consecutive negative blood test.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.reuters.com/article/health-ebola-guinea-idUSL8N13N0FV20151128#uBtDZJMYH0TtKLqF.97|title=Guinea's last Ebola case, a baby girl, leaves hospital|author=Reuters Editorial|date=28 November 2015|work=Reuters|access-date=29 November 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite report|title=Ebola Situation Report|date= 2 December 2015 |url=http://apps.who.int/ebola/current-situation/ebola-situation-report-2-december-2015|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20151208044152/http://apps.who.int/ebola/current-situation/ebola-situation-report-2-december-2015|url-status=dead|archive-date=8 December 2015|publisher=WHO}}</ref><ref>{{cite report|url=https://www.who.int/csr/disease/ebola/declaration-ebola-end/en/|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20141017223751/http://www.who.int/csr/disease/ebola/declaration-ebola-end/en/|url-status=dead|archive-date=17 October 2014|title=Criteria for declaring the end of the Ebola outbreak in Guinea, Liberia or Sierra Leone|publisher=WHO|access-date=10 December 2015}}</ref> The patient was discharged from the hospital on 28 November, per media reports<ref name=zoroya2015-11-17>{{cite news|title = Last known Ebola patient in West Africa recovers|url = https://www.usatoday.com/story/news/world/2015/11/17/last-known-ebola-patient-baby-girl-recovers/75916410/|newspaper= USA Today|access-date = 20 November 2015|last = Zoroya|first = Greg|date = 17 November 2015}}</ref>  on 29 December 2015, upon expiration of the 42-day waiting period, the WHO declared Guinea Ebola-free.<ref name="WHOend">{{cite news|title=End of Ebola transmission in Guinea |url=https://www.who.int/news-room/detail/29-12-2015-end-of-ebola-transmission-in-guinea |publisher= WHO  |access-date=6 March 2019 |language=en}}</ref>

On 17 March 2016, the government of Guinea reported, per the media, that 2 people had again tested positive for Ebola virus in [[Korokpara]],<ref name="Reuters2016">{{cite news|url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-health-ebola-guinea-idUSKCN0WJ2UQ|title=Guinea says two people tested positive for Ebola|work=Reuters|date=17 March 2016}}</ref> it was also reported that they were from the village where members of one family had recently died from vomiting (and diarrhea).<ref>{{cite magazine|url=http://time.com/4263806/two-people-test-positive-ebola-guinea/|title=2 Test Positive for Ebola in Guinea|last=Reilly|first=Katie|magazine=Time |access-date=2 April 2016}}</ref> On 19 March, it was also reported by the media that another individual had died due to the virus at the treatment centre in [[Nzerekore]],<ref>{{cite news|url=http://www.abc.net.au/news/2016-03-20/ebola-fourth-person-dies-in-guinea/7261234|title=Fourth person dies of Ebola in Guinea|newspaper=ABC News|publisher=ABC News Australia|language=en-AU|access-date=2 April 2016|date=2016-03-19}}</ref> consequently, the country's government quarantined an area around the home where the cases took place.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.yahoo.com/ebola-clinic-reopens-guinea-virus-resurfaces-140557643.html|title=Ebola clinic reopens in Guinea after virus resurfaces|publisher=Yahoo! news|access-date=2 April 2016}}</ref> On 22 March, the media reported that medical authorities in Guinea had quarantined 816 suspected contacts of the prior cases (more than 100 individuals were considered high-risk);<ref>{{cite report|url=https://www.who.int/csr/disease/ebola/guinea-flareup-update/en/|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160326081815/http://www.who.int/csr/disease/ebola/guinea-flareup-update/en/|url-status=dead|archive-date=26 March 2016|title=Hundreds of contacts identified and monitored in new Ebola flare-up in Guinea|publisher=WHO|language=en-GB|access-date=2 April 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/live/world-africa-35783318|title=Africa highlights: Tuesday 22 March 2016 as it happened |work=BBC News |access-date=2 April 2016}}</ref> the same day, Liberia ordered its border with Guinea closed.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.voanews.com/content/liberia-closes-boerder-with-guinea-after-ebola-flareup/3249034.html|title=Liberia Closes Border With Guinea After Ebola Flare-up |publisher=Voice of America|access-date=2 April 2016}}</ref> [[Macenta Prefecture]], {{convert|200|km}} from Korokpara, registered Guinea's fifth fatality due to Ebola virus disease within the same period.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-health-ebola-guinea-idUSKCN0WO2T1|title=Fifth person dies in Guinea Ebola flare-up|date=22 March 2016|work=Reuters|access-date=2 April 2016}}</ref> On 29 March, it was reported that about 1,000 contacts had been identified (142 of them high-risk),<ref name=EmergencyEnd>{{cite report|url=https://www.who.int/mediacentre/news/statements/2016/ihr-emergency-committee-ebola/en/|title=WHO Director-General briefs media on outcome of Ebola Emergency Committee|publisher=WHO|language=en-GB|access-date=2 April 2016}}</ref> and on 30 March 3 more confirmed cases were reported from the sub-prefecture of Koropara.<ref name="30who2016">{{cite report|url=http://apps.who.int/ebola/current-situation/ebola-situation-report-30-march-2016|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160401034733/http://apps.who.int/ebola/current-situation/ebola-situation-report-30-march-2016|url-status=dead|archive-date=1 April 2016|title=Ebola Situation Report |date=30 March 2016|publisher=WHO|access-date=9 June 2016}}</ref> On 1 April, it was reported by the media, that possible contacts, which numbered in the hundreds, had been vaccinated with an experimental vaccine using a [[ring vaccination]] approach.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.foxnews.com/health/2016/04/01/hundreds-in-guinea-get-ebola-vaccine-in-fight-against-flare-up.html|title=Hundreds in Guinea get Ebola vaccine in fight against flare-up|date=1 April 2016|publisher=Fox News|language=en-US|access-date=2 April 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite journal |last1=Kucharski |first1=Adam J. |last2=Eggo |first2=Rosalind M. |last3=Watson |first3=Conall H. |last4=Camacho |first4=Anton |last5=Funk |first5=Sebastian |last6=Edmunds |first6=W. John |title=Effectiveness of Ring Vaccination as Control Strategy for Ebola Virus Disease |journal=Emerging Infectious Diseases |date=2016 |volume=22 |issue=1 |pages=105–108 |doi=10.3201/eid2201.151410 |pmid=26691346 |pmc=4696719 }}</ref>

On 5 April 2016, it was reported via the media, that there had been 9 new cases of Ebola since the virus resurfaced, out of which 8 were fatal;<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.yahoo.com/news/ebola-claims-another-victim-guinea-vaccinations-ramped-192323781.html|title=Ebola claims another victim in Guinea as vaccinations ramped up|date=5 April 2016|publisher=Yahoo! News|language=en-US|access-date=6 April 2016}}</ref> on 1 June, after the stipulated waiting period, the WHO again declared Guinea Ebola-free,<ref name="guin">{{cite magazine|title=2 Test Positive for Ebola in Guinea |url=http://time.com/4263806/two-people-test-positive-ebola-guinea/ |magazine=Time |access-date=31 October 2018 |language=en}}</ref> after which the country entered a 90-day period of heightened surveillance that was concluded on 30 August 2016.

In September 2016, findings were published suggesting that the resurgence in Guinea was caused by an Ebola survivor who, after eight months of abstinence, had sexual relations with several partners, including the first victim in the new outbreak.<ref name="lurked">{{Cite journal|last1=Duraffour|first1=Sophie|last2=Rambaut|first2=Andrew|last3=Günther|first3=Stephan|last4=Keïta|first4=Sakoba|last5=Formenty|first5=Pierre|last6=Diarra|first6=Abdoulaye|last7=Djingarey|first7=Mamoudou Harouna|last8=Aylward|first8=Raymond Bruce|last9=Carroll|first9=Miles W.|date=15 November 2016|title=Resurgence of Ebola Virus Disease in Guinea Linked to a Survivor With Virus Persistence in Seminal Fluid for More Than 500 Days|journal=Clinical Infectious Diseases|volume=63|issue=10|pages=1353–1356|doi=10.1093/cid/ciw601|pmc=5091350|pmid=27585800}}</ref><ref name=BDiallo>{{cite journal |last1=Diallo |first1=Boubacar |last2=Sissoko |first2=Daouda |last3=Loman |first3=Nicholas J. |last4=Bah |first4=Hadja Aïssatou |last5=Bah |first5=Hawa |last6=Worrell |first6=Mary Claire |last7=Conde |first7=lya Saidou |last8=Sacko |first8=Ramata |last9=Mesfin |first9=Samuel |last10=Loua |first10=Angelo |last11=Kalonda |first11=Jacques Katomba |last12=Erondu |first12=Ngozi A. |last13=Dahl |first13=Benjamin A. |last14=Handrick |first14=Susann |last15=Goodfellow |first15=Ian |last16=Meredith |first16=Luke W. |last17=Cotten |first17=Matthew |last18=Jah |first18=Umaru |last19=Guetiya Wadoum |first19=Raoul Emeric |last20=Rollin |first20=Pierre |last21=Magassouba |first21=N'Faly |last22=Malvy |first22=Denis |last23=Anglaret |first23=Xavier |last24=Carroll |first24=Miles W. |last25=Aylward |first25=Raymond Bruce |last26=Djingarey |first26=Mamoudou Harouna |last27=Diarra |first27=Abdoulaye |last28=Formenty |first28=Pierre |last29=Keïta |first29=Sakoba |last30=Günther |first30=Stephan |last31=Rambaut |first31=Andrew |last32=Duraffour |first32=Sophie |title=Resurgence of Ebola Virus Disease in Guinea Linked to a Survivor With Virus Persistence in Seminal Fluid for More Than 500 Days |journal=Clinical Infectious Diseases |date=15 November 2016 |volume=63 |issue=10 |pages=1353–1356 |doi=10.1093/cid/ciw601|pmid=27585800|pmc=5091350}}</ref> The disease was also spread to Liberia by a woman who went there after her husband had died of Ebola.<ref name=discharge/>

==== Sierra Leone ====
{{Further|Ebola virus epidemic in Sierra Leone}}
[[File:Kenema Hospital Sierra Leone Ebola.JPG|thumb|Kenema Hospital, Sierra Leone]]
The first person reported infected in Sierra Leone, according to media reports, was a [[Traditional medicine|tribal healer]] who had been treating Ebola patients from across the nearby border with Guinea and who died on 26 May 2014; according to tribal tradition, her body was washed for burial, and this appears to have led to infections in women from neighbouring towns.<ref name="Fox News">{{cite news |url= http://www.foxnews.com/health/2014/08/25/sierra-leone-hero-doctor-death-exposes-slow-ebola-response/ |title= Sierra Leone 'hero' doctor's death exposes slow Ebola response |publisher= Fox News |date= 25 August 2014 |access-date= 25 August 2014}}</ref> On 11 June Sierra Leone shut its borders for trade with Guinea and Liberia and closed some schools in an attempt to slow the spread of the virus;<ref>{{cite news |url= http://uk.reuters.com/article/us-health-ebola-leone-idUKKBN0EM2CG20140611|title= Sierra Leone shuts borders, closes schools to fight Ebola |work= Reuters |date= 11 June 2014 | access-date= 11 April 2015}}</ref> on 30 July the government began to deploy troops to enforce quarantines,<ref>{{cite news |url= http://www.news24.com/Africa/News/Sierra-Leone-Liberia-deploy-troops-for-Ebola-20140804 |title= Sierra Leone, Liberia deploy troops for Ebola |publisher= News 24 |date= 4 August 2014 |access-date= 11 April 2015 |archive-date= 5 May 2019 |archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20190505224120/https://www.news24.com/Africa/News/Sierra-Leone-Liberia-deploy-troops-for-Ebola-20140804 |url-status= dead }}</ref> and by 15 October the last district in Sierra Leone previously untouched by the disease had declared Ebola cases.<ref>{{cite news|url= http://www.foxnews.com/world/2014/10/16/ebola-cases-appear-in-last-untouched-district-in-sierra-leone|title= Ebola cases appear in last untouched district in Sierra Leone|publisher= Fox News|date= 16 October 2014|access-date= 16 October 2014}}</ref>

During the first week of November reports told of a worsening situation due to intense transmission in Freetown. According to the Disaster Emergency Committee, food shortages resulting from aggressive quarantines were making the situation worse,<ref>{{cite web|url= https://news.vice.com/article/the-ebola-outbreak-is-getting-worse-in-sierra-leone|title= The Ebola Outbreak Is Getting Worse in Sierra Leone|publisher= VICE News|access-date= 10 November 2014|date= 2014-11-06}}</ref> and on 4 November media reported that thousands had violated quarantine in search of food in the town of [[Kenema]].<ref>{{cite web|url= http://www.detroitnews.com/story/news/world/2014/11/04/ebola-west-africa/18463943/|title= Thousands in Sierra Leone break Ebola quarantine|first1= Sarah |last1= DiLorenzo|date= 4 November 2014|publisher= Associated Press|access-date= 5 November 2014}}</ref> With the number of cases continuing to increase, an MSF coordinator described the situation in Sierra Leone as "catastrophic", saying, "there are several villages and communities that have been basically wiped out&nbsp;... Whole communities have disappeared but many of them are not in the statistics." In mid-November the WHO reported that, while there was some evidence that the number of cases were no longer rising in Guinea and Liberia, steep increases persisted in Sierra Leone.<ref name=":5" />
[[File:Ebola crisis- More UK aid arrives in Sierra Leone (15327635047).jpg|thumb|Ebola crisis: More UK aid arrives in Sierra Leone]]
On 9 December 2014 news reports described the discovery of "a grim scene"—piles of bodies, overwhelmed medical personnel and exhausted burial teams—in the remote eastern [[Kono District]].<ref>{{cite news|url= http://www.abc.net.au/news/2014-12-11/sierra-leone-hit-by-largely-hidden-ebola-outbreak/5959596|title= Ebola crisis: Sierra Leone hit by largely hidden outbreak; WHO says scores of bodies piled up|work= ABC News|access-date= 11 December 2014|date= 2014-12-10}}</ref>  On 15 December the [[Centers for Disease Control and Prevention|CDC]] indicated that their main concern was Sierra Leone, where the epidemic had shown no signs of abating as cases continued to rise exponentially; by the second week of December, Sierra Leone had reported nearly 400&nbsp;cases—more than three times the number reported by Guinea and Liberia combined. According to the CDC, "the risk we face now [is] that Ebola will simmer along, become native and be a problem for Africa and the world, for years to come".<ref>{{cite news|url= https://www.npr.org/blogs/goatsandsoda/2014/12/15/370446566/endless-ebola-endemic-thats-the-risk-we-face-now-cdc-says|title= Endless Ebola Epidemic? That's The 'Risk We Face Now,' CDC Says|date= 15 December 2014|newspaper= NPR |access-date= 18 December 2014|last1= Doucleff|first1= Michaeleen}}</ref>  On 17 December [[Ernest Bai Koroma|President Koroma]] of Sierra Leone launched "Operation Western Area Surge" and workers went door-to-door in the capital city looking for possible cases.<ref name="Ebola_Outbreak_total_sl_14_Dec">{{cite report|publisher= Sierra Leone Ministry of Health and Sanitation| url= http://health.gov.sl/wp-content/uploads/2014/12/Ebola-Situation-Report_Vol-201.pdf| title= Sierra Leone: Ebola Virus Disease – Situation Report| access-date= 15 December 2014| date= 15 December 2014| url-status= dead| archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20141220203935/http://health.gov.sl/wp-content/uploads/2014/12/Ebola-Situation-Report_Vol-201.pdf| archive-date= 20 December 2014| df= dmy-all}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|url= https://www.bbc.com/news/world-africa-30511208|title= Ebola: Sierra Leone begins house-to-house searches|work= BBC News|access-date= 18 December 2014|date= 2014-12-17}}</ref>  The operation led to a surge in reports of cases, with 403&nbsp;new ones reported between 14&nbsp;and&nbsp;17 December.<ref name=Ebola_Outbreak_total_sl_14_Dec /><ref name="Ebola_Outbreak_total_sl_18_Dec">{{cite report|publisher= Sierra Leone Ministry of Health and Sanitation| url= http://health.gov.sl/wp-content/uploads/2014/12/Ebola-Situation-Report_Vol-204.pdf| title= Ebola Virus Disease – Situation Report| access-date= 19 December 2014| date= 18 December 2014| url-status= dead| archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20141219161011/http://health.gov.sl/wp-content/uploads/2014/12/Ebola-Situation-Report_Vol-204.pdf| archive-date= 19 December 2014| df= dmy-all}}</ref>

According to the 21 January 2015 WHO Situation Report, the case [[Incidence (epidemiology)|incidence]] was rapidly decreasing in Sierra Leone.<ref>{{cite magazine|title= Ebola Could be 'Levelling Off' in Sierra Leone: WHO|url= http://www.newsweek.com/ebola-could-be-levelling-sierra-leone-who-297831|magazine= Newsweek|date= 8 January 2015|access-date= 11 January 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|url= http://www.csmonitor.com/World/Latest-News-Wires/2015/0114/Sierra-Leone-predicts-no-new-Ebola-cases-by-March-end-video|title= Sierra Leone predicts no new Ebola cases by March end (+video)|work= Christian Science Monitor|publisher= The Christian Science Monitor|access-date= 15 January 2015|date= 2015-01-14}}</ref><ref>{{cite report |title= Ebola Situation Report | date= 21 January 2015 |url= http://apps.who.int/ebola/en/status-outbreak/situation-reports/ebola-situation-report-21-january-2015 |archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20150201050920/http://apps.who.int/ebola/en/status-outbreak/situation-reports/ebola-situation-report-21-january-2015 |url-status= dead |archive-date= 1 February 2015 |publisher= WHO|access-date= 27 January 2019}}</ref> However, in February and March reports indicated a rise again in the number of cases.<ref>{{cite news|url= https://www.usatoday.com/story/news/world/2015/02/05/ebola-liberia-sierra-leone-guinea-infections-increase/22935171/|title= Downward Ebola trend suddenly reverses itself|author= Gregg Zoroya|date= 5 February 2015|newspaper= USA Today|access-date= 6 February 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url= http://www.voanews.com/content/ebola-hit-sierra-leone-to-reopen-schools-march-3oth/2629854.html|title= Ebola-hit Sierra Leone to Reopen Schools March 30|publisher= VOA|access-date= 7 February 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url= http://www.philstar.com/world/2015/02/21/1426253/decline-ebola-cases-flattens-raising-un-concern|title= Decline in Ebola cases flattens, raising UN concern|publisher= Philadelphia Star |access-date= 22 February 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url= http://www.gnnliberia.com/articles/2015/03/05/more-ebola-guinea-sierra-leone-last-week-no-liberia-cases-says-who|archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20150402093450/http://www.gnnliberia.com/articles/2015/03/05/more-ebola-guinea-sierra-leone-last-week-no-liberia-cases-says-who|archive-date= 2 April 2015|title= More Ebola in Guinea, Sierra Leone last week, no Liberia cases says WHO|publisher= gnnliberia.com|access-date= 7 March 2015}}</ref>  The following month, the 5 April WHO report again disclosed a downward trend<ref>{{cite web|url= http://www.voanews.com/content/lowest-weekly-figure-of-ebola-cases-reported-in-nearly-a-year/2711801.html|title= Lowest Weekly Figure of Ebola Cases Reported in Nearly a Year|publisher= VOA|access-date= 10 April 2015}}</ref> and the WHO weekly update for 29 July reported a total of only 3 new cases, the lowest in more than a year.<ref name=":4" /> On 17 August the country marked its first week with no new cases,<ref>{{cite magazine|url= http://time.com/4000158/sierra-leone-no-new-ebola/|title= Sierra Leone Has First Week of No New Ebola Cases|author= Alexandra Sifferlin|magazine= Time |access-date= 19 August 2015|date= 17 August 2015}}</ref> and one week later the last patients were released.<ref>[https://www.un.org/apps/news/story.asp?NewsID=51732#.Vd7mcTZRFpg Sierra Leone begins 42-day countdown to be declared free of Ebola virus transmission]. ''UN News Centre''. 26 August 2015.</ref>  However, a new case emerged on 1 September, when a patient from Sella Kafta village in [[Kambia District]] tested positive for the disease after her death;<ref>{{cite news|url= http://www.news24.com/Africa/News/New-Ebola-death-in-Sierra-Leone-sets-back-efforts-to-beat-epidemic-20150831|title= New Ebola death in Sierra Leone sets back efforts to beat epidemic|publisher= News 24|access-date= 1 September 2015|date= 1 September 2015 }}</ref> her case eventually resulted in 3 other infections among her contacts.<ref>{{cite news|url= https://www.usnews.com/news/world/articles/2015/09/08/sierra-leone-officials-confirm-3-new-cases-of-ebola |title= Sierra Leone officials confirm 3 new cases of Ebola among high risk contacts with fatal case |agency= Associated Press |access-date= 9 September 2015 |date= 8 September 2015 |url-status= dead |archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20151121075747/http://www.usnews.com/news/world/articles/2015/09/08/sierra-leone-officials-confirm-3-new-cases-of-ebola |archive-date= 21 November 2015 }}</ref>

On 14 September 2015 Sierra Leone's National Ebola Response Centre confirmed the death of a 16-year-old in a village in the [[Bombali District]].<ref name="auto6">{{cite news|url= http://www.ctvnews.ca/health/new-ebola-death-reported-in-northern-sierra-leone-1.2562302|title= New Ebola death reported in northern Sierra Leone|publisher= CTV News|access-date= 14 September 2015|date= 14 September 2015 }}</ref> It is suspected that she contracted the disease from the semen of an Ebola survivor who had been discharged in March 2015.<ref name="auto7">{{cite news|url= https://www.reuters.com/article/us-health-ebola-leone-idUSKCN0RE1P620150914|title= Hundreds quarantined as Ebola returns to north Sierra Leone district|work= Reuters|access-date= 14 September 2015|date= 14 September 2015 }}</ref> On 27 September a new 42-day countdown began to declare the country Ebola-free,<ref>{{cite web|url= http://www.voanews.com/content/sierra-leone-begins-new-ebola-42-day-countdown/2982177.html|title= Sierra Leone Begins New Ebola 42-day Countdown|publisher= VOA|access-date= 30 September 2015}}</ref> which eventually occurred on 7 November 2015; thereafter, the country increased its vigilance on the Guinean border.<ref>{{cite web|url= http://www.voanews.com/content/anticipation-grows-as-sierra-leone-readies-to-be-declared-ebola-free/3041603.html|title= Anticipation Grows as Sierra Leone Readies to be Declared Ebola-free|publisher= VOA|access-date= 8 November 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite report|url= http://apps.who.int/ebola/current-situation/ebola-situation-report-11-november-2015|archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20151111211316/http://apps.who.int/ebola/current-situation/ebola-situation-report-11-november-2015|url-status= dead|archive-date= 11 November 2015|title= Ebola Situation Report | date= 11 November 2015|publisher= WHO|access-date= 27 January 2016}}</ref>

Sierra Leone had entered a 90-day period of enhanced surveillance that was scheduled to end on 5 February 2016, when, on 14 January, a new Ebola death was reported in the [[Tonkolili District]].<ref>{{cite web|url= http://apps.who.int/ebola/current-situation/ebola-situation-report-9-december-2015|archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20151211130610/http://apps.who.int/ebola/current-situation/ebola-situation-report-9-december-2015|url-status= dead|archive-date= 11 December 2015|title= Ebola Situation Report | date= 9 December 2015|access-date= 17 December 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|url= https://www.bbc.com/news/world-africa-35320363|title= Ebola virus: New case emerges in Sierra Leone|work= BBC News|date= 2016-01-15}}</ref> Prior to this case, the WHO had advised that "we still anticipate more flare-ups and must be prepared for them. A massive effort is underway to ensure robust prevention, surveillance and response capacity across all three countries by the end of March."<ref>{{cite report|url=https://www.who.int/mediacentre/news/releases/2016/ebola-zero-liberia/en/|title= Latest Ebola outbreak over in Liberia; West Africa is at zero, but new flare-ups are likely to occur|publisher= WHO}}</ref> On 16 January aid workers reported that a woman had died of the virus and that she may have exposed several individuals; the government later announced that 100 people had been quarantined.<ref>{{cite news|url= https://www.theguardian.com/world/2016/jan/15/ebola-victim-in-sierra-leone-feared-to-have-exposed-27-others-to-virus|title= Sierra Leone puts more than 100 people in quarantine after new Ebola death|newspaper= The Guardian|date= 2016-01-17}}</ref> Investigations indicated that the deceased was a female student from [[Lunsar]], in [[Port Loko District]], who had gone to [[Kambia District]] on 28 December 2015 before returning symptomatic. She had also visited Bombali District to consult a herbalist, and had later gone to a government hospital in [[Magburaka]]. The WHO indicated that there were 109&nbsp;contacts (28 of them high-risk), that there were another 3&nbsp;missing contacts, and that the source or route of transmission that caused the fatality was unknown.<ref>{{cite report |url= http://www.afro.who.int/en/sierra-leone/press-materials/item/8281-government-press-statement-confirmation-of-evd-death-in-sierra-leone-–-16-january-2016.html |title= Government Press Statement: Confirmation of EVD Death in Sierra Leone |publisher= WHO |date= 16 January 2016 |access-date= 21 January 2016 |url-status= dead |archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20160122004724/http://www.afro.who.int/en/sierra-leone/press-materials/item/8281-government-press-statement-confirmation-of-evd-death-in-sierra-leone-%E2%80%93-16-january-2016.html |archive-date= 22 January 2016 |df= dmy-all }}</ref> A second new case—confirmed by WHO spokesman Tarik Jasarevic to involve a 38-year-old relative and caregiver of the aforementioned Ebola victim—had become symptomatic on 20 Jan while under observation at a quarantine centre.<ref>{{cite news | url= http://www.itv.com/news/update/2016-01-20/sierra-leone-confirms-second-case-of-ebola-in-a-week/ |title= Sierra Leone confirms second case of Ebola in a week |publisher= Yahoo! News |date= 20 January 2016 |access-date= 21 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite report|url= http://www.aljazeera.com/news/2016/01/fear-sierra-leone-ebola-case-confirmed-160121055559943.html|title= Ebola in Sierra Leone: New case spreads community fear|publisher= WHO|access-date= 22 January 2016}}</ref> On 22 January it was reported that this patient was responding to treatment.<ref>{{cite web|url= https://news.yahoo.com/sierra-leone-ebola-case-responding-treatment-222558577.html|title= New Sierra Leone Ebola case responding to treatment|date= 22 January 2016|publisher= Yahoo! News|access-date= 27 January 2016}}</ref> On 26 January WHO Director-General, Dr&nbsp;Margaret Chan officially confirmed that the outbreak was not yet over;<ref name="who.int1"/> that same day, it was also reported that Ebola restrictions had halted market activity in Kambia District amid protests.<ref>{{cite web|url= https://abcnews.go.com/Health/wireStory/sierra-leone-youth-protest-ebola-restrictions-36530631|title= Health Index|work= ABC News|access-date= 9 June 2016}}</ref> On 7 February 70&nbsp;individuals were released from quarantine,<ref>{{cite web|url= http://learningenglish.voanews.com/content/sierra-leone-releases-ebola-quarantine/3178930.html|title= Sierra Leone Releases 70 from Ebola Quarantine|publisher= VOA |access-date= 9 June 2016}}</ref> and on 8 February the last Ebola patient was also released.<ref>{{cite news|url= https://www.reuters.com/article/us-health-ebola-leone-idUSKCN0VH1ZD|title= Sierra Leone discharges last known Ebola patient|date= 8 February 2016|work= Reuters |access-date= 9 June 2016}}</ref> On 17 February the WHO indicated that 2,600 Ebola survivors had accessed health assessments and eye examinations.<ref name="16who161">{{cite report |title= Latest Ebola outbreak over in Liberia; West Africa is at zero, but new flare-ups are likely to occur |url=https://www.who.int/en/news-room/detail/14-01-2016-latest-ebola-outbreak-over-in-liberia-west-africa-is-at-zero-but-new-flare-ups-are-likely-to-occur |publisher= WHO |access-date= 30 October 2018}}</ref>

On 4 February 2016 the last known case tested negative for a second consecutive time and Sierra Leone commenced another 42-day countdown towards being declared Ebola-free.<ref>{{cite report|url= http://apps.who.int/ebola/current-situation/ebola-situation-report-17-february-2016|archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20160220015215/http://apps.who.int/ebola/current-situation/ebola-situation-report-17-february-2016|url-status= dead|archive-date= 20 February 2016|title= Ebola Situation Report |date= 17 February 2016|publisher= WHO |access-date= 9 June 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite report|url=https://www.who.int/mediacentre/news/statements/2016/end-flare-ebola-sierra-leone/en/|title= WHO statement on end of Ebola flare-up in Sierra Leone|publisher= WHO |access-date= 9 June 2016}}</ref> On 17 March 2016 the WHO announced that the Sierra Leone flare-up was over, and that no other chains of transmission were known to be active at that time.<ref>{{cite web|url= https://news.yahoo.com/sierra-leone-ebola-flare-over-virus-no-longer-093953051.html|title= Sierra Leone Ebola flare-up over, virus no longer spreading: WHO|publisher= Yahoo! News|access-date= 17 March 2016}}</ref> The media reported that Sierra Leone then entered a 90-day period of heightened surveillance, which concluded on 15 June 2016, and it was reported that by 15 July the country had discontinued testing corpses for the virus.<ref>
{{cite web
|title= Sierra Leone Stops Mandatory Testing Of Corpses For Ebola
|url= http://www.ndtv.com/world-news/sierra-leone-stops-mandatory-testing-of-corpses-for-ebola-1431971
|publisher= Agence France Presse|access-date= 1 August 2016
}}
</ref>

==== Liberia ====
{{Further|Ebola virus epidemic in Liberia}}
[[File:Ebola Treatment Unit.jpg|thumb|An Ebola treatment unit in Liberia]]
In Liberia, the disease was reported in both [[Lofa County|Lofa]] and [[Nimba County|Nimba]] counties in late March 2014.<ref name="liberianobserver.com">{{cite news|url=http://www.liberianobserver.com/security-health/2-5-test-positive-ebola-liberia |title=2 of 5 Test Positive for Ebola in Liberia |publisher=Liberian Observer |date=31 March 2014 |access-date=6 July 2014 |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140709004219/http://www.liberianobserver.com/security-health/2-5-test-positive-ebola-liberia |archive-date= 9 July 2014 }}</ref>  On 27 July, [[Ellen Johnson Sirleaf|President Ellen Johnson Sirleaf]] announced that Liberia would close its borders, with the exception of a few crossing points such as [[Roberts International Airport]], where screening centres would be established.<ref name=BBC_28_July_2014>{{cite news |url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-africa-28522824 |title=Ebola outbreak: Liberia shuts most border points |work=BBC News |date=28 July 2014 |access-date=28 July 2014}}</ref> Schools and universities were closed,<ref>{{cite news|last=Kwanue|first=C.Y.|url=http://www.liberianobserver.com/security/compliance-sirleaf%E2%80%99s-mandate-ul-closed|title=In Compliance with Sirleaf's Mandate, UL Closed|publisher=Liberian Observer|date=1 August 2014|access-date=2 August 2014|url-status=dead|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140808051313/http://www.liberianobserver.com/security/compliance-sirleaf%E2%80%99s-mandate-ul-closed|archive-date=8 August 2014|df=dmy-all}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.reuters.com/article/health-ebola-africa-idUSL6N0Q56DX20140730|title=Liberia shuts schools, quarantines communities in bid to halt Ebola|work=Reuters|date=30 July 2014|access-date=30 July 2014}}</ref> and the worst-affected areas in the country were placed under quarantine.<ref name="BBC_28_July_20142">{{cite news |url = https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-africa-28522824|title = Ebola outbreak: Liberia shuts most border points|work= BBC News|date = 28 July 2014|access-date = 28 July 2014}}</ref>

With only 50 physicians in the entire country—one for every 70,000&nbsp;citizens—Liberia was already in a healthcare crisis.<ref name=":6">{{cite news| url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-africa-29516663 | title=Ebola outbreak: Liberia 'close to collapse' – ambassador | publisher=BBC News Africa | author=Katty, Kay | date=7 October 2014 | access-date=8 October 2014}}</ref>  In September, the [[Centers for Disease Control and Prevention|CDC]] reported that some hospitals had been abandoned, while those still functioning lacked basic facilities and supplies.<ref>{{cite web|title=Runaway Doctors and Missing Supplies Cripple Care in Ebola-Hit Liberia|url=http://www.nbcnews.com/storyline/ebola-virus-outbreak/runaway-doctors-missing-supplies-cripple-care-ebola-hit-liberia-n220686|work=NBC News|access-date=8 October 2014}}</ref>  In October, the Liberian ambassador in Washington was reported as saying that he feared that his country may be "close to collapse";<ref name=":6" />  by 24 October, all [[counties of Liberia|15 counties]] had reported Ebola cases.<ref name="WHO20141022">{{cite report|url = http://apps.who.int/iris/bitstream/10665/137091/1/roadmapsitrep22Oct2014_eng.pdf|access-date = 22 October 2014|title = Ebola Response Roadmap Situation Report|date = 22 October 2014|publisher= WHO}}</ref><ref name="Ebola_Outbreak_total_lr_24_Oct">{{cite report |publisher= Liberia Ministry of Health and Social Welfare|url=http://www.mohsw.gov.lr/documents/SITREP%20162%20Oct%2024th%202014_1.pdf |title=Liberia Ebola SitRep no. 157 |access-date=24 October 2014 |date=24 October 2014 |url-status=dead |archive-url=http://webarchive.loc.gov/all/20141204105311/http://www.mohsw.gov.lr/documents/SITREP%20162%20Oct%2024th%202014_1.pdf |archive-date=4 December 2014 |df=dmy-all }}</ref>

By November 2014, the rate of new infections in Liberia appeared to be declining and the state of emergency was lifted.
